Social Miscellany

Gang Fight

Yesterday morning at around 8:00 AM, a large gang suddenly started fighting at the intersection of Rue Robert and Rue Pignan in western Shanghai. At the time, the two sides had a total of thirty to forty gangsters gathered, arranged in formations, each wielding lethal weapons such as iron rods, iron rulers, knives, and axes. Pedestrians, seeing this, fled in alarm. As a result, many people on both sides were injured. It is said that the gang fight was caused by a feud between local gangs and gangs from Jiangbei.

Apprentice Injured

Kang Zhicai, an apprentice at the Xinchang Machinery Factory located at 1212 Avenue Edward VII, a sixteen-year-old native of Ningbo, was working at around 2:30 PM yesterday when, due to a moment's carelessness, his body was caught in a machine belt, lifted into the air, and his chest and arms were crushed. He was later rescued by his companions and taken to the hospital for treatment.

Zhu Qihui's Memorial Service Today

Mr. Zhu Qihui of Baoying, a member of a distinguished scholarly family, had resided in Shanghai for many years. Since the sudden outbreak of the August 13th Shanghai Battle, Mr. Zhu suffered from asthma and suddenly passed away. His eldest son, Yinyu, who was away from home on business at the time, rushed back upon hearing the news. Upholding his father's last wishes, the funeral arrangements were kept simple. The remains were temporarily placed at the Jiangning Guild Hall. Originally, it was planned to choose a date to escort the coffin back home for burial and mourning. However, as Baoying has fallen, there is no hope of returning for burial. Moreover, the second anniversary of his death is approaching, and the mourning period will soon be over. A memorial service will be held today (the 10th) in Kuling. All relatives and friends are expected to attend, making it a grand occasion.

Letter to the Editor

To the Editor: We have read in your newspaper's local news column on the 6th of this month a news item titled "Opium Paraphernalia Confiscated from the National Correspondence School." The content vaguely states that someone had privately set up an opium den at the Qifeng Chinese Painting Correspondence School at No. 443 and 445 Kangti Road, and that opium paraphernalia and a pot of opium paste were confiscated from the principal's office, and that a woman named Gu Tong from Anhui and others were arrested. We are extremely shocked. According to our school, which has been established for many years and has already been approved and registered by the education authorities, our school's family members and others conduct themselves with integrity. We have neither established an opium den nor have any bad habits. However, there are many tenants living in the same building, and it is possible that some of them may possess opium paraphernalia. As for the confiscation of opium paraphernalia from the principal's office, this is completely unfounded. This matter concerns the reputation of our school, so we are writing this letter to request that your newspaper grant us a correction in the "Letters to the Editor" column, so as to avoid confusion and rumors. This is our sincere request. Sincerely, The Qifeng Chinese Painting Correspondence School, December 9th.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that Shandong and this area will be sunny and cold with strong, biting northwesterly winds. The East China Sea will be sunny with strong, biting northerly to easterly winds. The center of the hurricane moved to within 120 miles of 16 degrees north latitude and 131 degrees east longitude yesterday afternoon, stopped moving forward, or deviated to the north to northeast. The wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 62.6 degrees, and the lowest was 41.0 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 6.1 degrees, and the lowest was 51.0 degrees.

Education News

Ministry of Education's Plan to Improve Frontier Education (Part 2): Defining Frontier Education Guidelines and Central Objectives; Cultivating Teachers and Compiling Teaching Materials

(D) Promoting Frontier School Education

(1) Elementary education shall be based on primary schools, divided into fixed and mobile types, to adapt to the frontier environment. (2) Primary schools shall be established by local authorities in principle, with subsidies from the central government as appropriate. However, the Ministry of Education may establish frontier experimental primary schools in appropriate locations on the frontier for the purpose of experimentation and guidance of elementary education in its jurisdiction. (3) Primary and secondary schools shall enroll students from all ethnic groups in the area and shall use the name of the location as the school name. (4) Various facilities in frontier secondary schools shall comply with the regulations of the Ministry of Education. However, in order to adapt to frontier conditions, both junior and senior high schools may be extended by one year to provide simplified normal, simplified vocational, local autonomy, health administration, cooperative, and reclamation association training. (5) In impoverished provinces that cannot establish secondary schools, the Ministry of Education shall establish or subsidize their establishment, and may request relevant agencies (such as the Boxer Indemnity Management Agency) to provide subsidies as appropriate. (6) Education administrative agencies in frontier provinces may establish vocational schools at all levels as needed. The Ministry of Education shall also establish vocational schools at all levels in suitable locations to meet the desire of inland youth to work in the frontier. The central government shall provide subsidies for equipment and start-up costs. Establish universities, independent colleges, or specialized schools in appropriate locations on the frontier. (7) Establish a National Frontier Affairs University or Frontier College, focusing on cultivation, various construction projects, medicine and health, national language, religion, philosophy, science, surveying, and other departments, in order to cultivate talents for frontier construction and religious talents with new ideas. (8) The Ministry of Education may designate national universities to increase relevant departments related to frontier construction and elective courses in frontier languages as appropriate. Approved colleges and universities that wish to add such departments may request subsidies from the Ministry of Education or local education administrative agencies with their prior consent. (9) Frontier youths who are admitted to inland colleges and universities shall be allowed to take separate entrance examinations. Those who cannot study all the courses shall be allowed to select several required courses. (10) Conduct training classes for frontier cadres to train cadres and staff for frontier education work.

(E) Promoting Frontier Social Education

(1) The Ministry of Education shall establish several frontier mobile education work groups to tour the frontier areas to varying degrees, using medicine, music, film, and books as teaching tools. Provinces should also establish frontier mobile education work groups as needed. (2) For the purpose of experimenting with the overall facilities of frontier education, the Ministry of Education may divide the frontier areas into several frontier education experimental zones, and first designate one or two zones to implement frontier experimental education, and then gradually promote it. (3) Establish a frontier cultural center to collect various political, economic, cultural, scientific, historical materials, statistics, charts, photos, specimens, models, and books from the frontier to provide reference for those who study frontier issues and to inspire the people of the country to build the frontier. (4) Temples should be attached to public schools or half-day schools, and use scripture lectures to conduct literacy campaigns and spiritual talks. For Arabic schools, they should be required to add one hour of national language, half an hour of common sense, and half an hour of arithmetic per day. (5) Increase the distribution of radios and educational film projectors in various frontier areas. (6) Frontier provinces and counties should establish libraries and public education centers in accordance with regulations, and the funding should be raised locally, with subsidies from the Ministry of Education as appropriate.

(F) Establishing a Frontier Education Encouragement System

(1) Frontier schools at all levels, with the special approval of the Ministry of Education, may appoint a supervisor in addition to the principal. (2) Frontier local education administrative agencies may, depending on local needs, hire local enthusiastic educators to serve as education promoters. Education promoters are voluntary positions, and those with outstanding achievements will be given appropriate rewards. (3) Frontier students may be given stipends and bonuses as appropriate, or exempted from their corresponding corvée labor. (4) Colleges and universities should set up more public-funded places for frontier students. (5) Stipends and subsidies for students at all levels in the frontier should be allocated in a coordinated and preferential manner to maintain a minimum standard of living, so as to enable them to study with peace of mind, and to improve the treatment of faculty and staff at all levels in the frontier to encourage aspiring youth to actively participate in frontier work. (6) The assessment and reward of personnel serving in the frontier should be formulated to achieve effective results. (End)

Business News

Food: Can We End the People's Woe and Sorrow, And Let Hoarders Make a Fortune? Market Sits and Profits from Each Transaction, Small People Shed Blood and Tears for Every Unit of Grain, Prices Rise Without End

According to reports, the rice market opened early yesterday with about 14 or 15 trucks of goods arriving near the Suzhou-Jiading Road area. Sellers continued to hold back, refusing to show samples. As soon as inquiries were made, prices soared. Regardless of whether it was japonica or indica rice, the price was called up by more than two yuan in an instant, and ordinary japonica rice even reached nearly 49 yuan. The higher it was raised, the higher it went. The situation rebounded again at noon. This has been the consistent style of the rice market in recent days. A large number of transactions have already been completed, and hoarders are manipulating the market from selling to profiting. Only the working class suffers, struggling to buy a liter of rice with the sweat of their labor, watching helplessly as unscrupulous merchants freely manipulate the market and make a fortune without any prevention. In fact, as long as the arrivals are investigated from various import and export sources, all the rice that arrives is concentrated in the market, and purchased by various rice shops to meet market demand. The market price is determined publicly according to the quantity of arrivals and the needs of the market, and everyone must abide by it. It is absolutely forbidden to hoard rice in warehouses. If this method is followed, the price of rice can be stabilized immediately in a few days. On the one hand, thoroughly investigate the rice stored in various public and private warehouses, and on the other hand, investigate the fixed amount of foreign rice with various foreign firms, and order the rice industry to report the orders. Then, discuss the entire food management method. Even if the food situation in Shanghai cannot be restored to its previous state, there will eventually be a day of stability. How can we remain indifferent and inactive? At the close of the market yesterday, prices rose by half a yuan to nearly one yuan, regardless of japonica or indica rice. Special japonica rice from the Changbang area was 48 yuan, middle japonica rice was 46 to 47 yuan, and Saigon rice was 39 yuan and 38.5 yuan.

Early in the morning, Ke Xian rice soared in unison with other types of rice, rising by another one or two yuan compared to the previous market. It was then sold by floating profit-takers. Moreover, there were two full shipments of foreign rice, and Ke Xian rice has recently been arriving in Shanghai from the Jiangxi, Beijing, Wuhu, and Hankou areas, and raw rice is also being transported in an endless stream. Therefore, the market turned flat later in the day. However, it still rose by seven or eight cents compared to the previous day.

New foreign rice is difficult to allocate. Several previous telegrams have not been replied to, but most of the orders have been loaded. Yesterday, there were 25,000 bags being unloaded, and another 22,000 bags arrived in Pudong waiting to be unloaded. In the early morning, the spot market was once again manipulated and inflated by hoarders and speculators, and Saigon rice was once called up to 40 yuan. The result was 39 yuan. Relocated road cargo gradually became lively. Yesterday's total turnover was 745 tons, with prices ranging from 45.5 yuan to 46.1 yuan, all calculated by the original package.

Another 3,640 bags of newly arrived foreign rice arrived yesterday morning, transported from Rangoon by the Taikoo Company's New Beijing ship. It is said that the ship also carries a lot of foreign rice bound for North China, but the exact number is unknown.

The trend of flour yesterday was peaceful, because after repeated increases, actual sales gradually cleared. Cash Stagnation: Fluctuations Only a Few Dozen Yuan

Yesterday, the cash market was tepid and unclear. Due to the stagnation of foreign exchange, fluctuations were minimal, only rising and falling by about ten yuan. However, the underlying trend was firm. Although some money changers continued to release cash and some gold shops sold on behalf of speculators, the Hong Kong syndicate frequently commissioned certain silver shops to handle transactions, and the volume was considerable. Ultimately, the price rose by ten yuan, opening ten yuan higher at 4,180 yuan. Subsequently, as the foreign exchange market softened slightly, coupled with purchases by certain securities firms and the Hong Kong syndicate, the price briefly rose to 4,200 yuan. However, the foreign exchange market suddenly reported a return to par, and the selling intentions of some money changers and gold shops intensified. Although the Hong Kong syndicate continued to buy, many general long positions also closed, making it difficult to match the supply. As a result, the price returned to 4,180 yuan at the noon close, the same as the morning opening. In the afternoon, the off-exchange trend continued to strengthen, as gold shops absorbed supply previously, and some money changers followed suit. It was rumored that the final price was 4,188 yuan, with over 2,000 taels traded during the half-day session. Silver shop jewelry was priced five yuan higher, while customs gold remained flat.

Tepid Market Rises Ten Yuan

From the morning, each bar (ten taels) opened quietly and firmly. At 9:35 AM, the market opened ten yuan higher, with money changers buying 50 taels from gold shops at 4,180 yuan. Subsequently, a silver shop bought on behalf of a client, raising the price by another ten yuan, with money changers trading ten taels at 4,190 yuan. At that time, securities firms released dozens of taels, and silver shops also sold, causing a drop of ten yuan. Securities firms sold 50 taels to gold shops at 4,180 yuan. Later, due to the steady and slightly soft foreign exchange market, some securities firms and others came to the market to buy. Soon, the Hong Kong syndicate commissioned a silver shop to buy again, raising the price by another twenty yuan, with securities firms buying 30 taels from other firms at 4,200 yuan. When the Hong Kong syndicate stopped buying, the price immediately fell. Gold shops and money changers mutually helped large clients to sell, and soon the price fell another twenty yuan, with gold shops selling twenty taels to money changers at 4,180 yuan. Later, a silver shop again bought on behalf of the Hong Kong syndicate, raising the price by ten yuan, with money changers buying twenty taels from securities firms at 4,190 yuan. At noon, securities firms continued to release supply, and at the same time, some gold shops and others were still willing to sell, so the silver shop suddenly gave up, quoting the price at 4,185 yuan. The silver shop then absorbed 160 taels from a gold shop and dozens of taels from retail investors. Later, as the Hong Kong syndicate was satisfied with its purchases, the price fell back by five yuan, with money changers mutually trading twenty taels at 4,180 yuan, as the noon closing price. As a result, the market rose by ten yuan compared to the previous day, with only a twenty yuan fluctuation in the half-day session. The selling price of cash gold shops was a few yuan higher than the tepid market, and the buying price was reduced by about twenty yuan. Spot gold was over fifty yuan lower than the listed gold price, with few transactions.

Guangdong Syndicate's Demand for Single Yarn Recovers, 20-Count Yarn Still Has Thick Inventory, Nothing More Than Being Driven Up by Raw Materials

Sugar Market: Diaoqing Rises Two Yuan

Yesterday, the sugar market was tightest for domestic Diaoqing, with a total of 2,000 bags opened at a price of 30 yuan, up about two yuan. Chao syndicate also opened dozens of bags of Huanggangqing at 40 yuan and 7 jiao, an increase of 7 jiao. The Public Association's foreign sugar market saw mixed rises and falls. Spot 24 crude white slightly fell, with the local warehouse at 55 yuan 7 jiao to 56 yuan 3 jiao, and new goods at the foreign warehouse at 57 yuan and old goods at 56 yuan 7 jiao to 8 jiao. However, transit goods rose again by one yuan due to the Hong Kong syndicate's appetite, with a price of 47 yuan and a half to 48 yuan, with 400 bags traded. Taikoo White also fell by a small half yuan, B Mark East Warehouse 55 and a half yuan, West Warehouse 56 yuan, and the rest remained unchanged, H Mark Che Chi 40 yuan, He Chi 41 yuan to 41 and a half yuan. This cotton white and No. 1 ice are lacking in change. It was found that 1,635 bags of sugar came from Hong Kong yesterday.

Medicinal Materials: New White Chrysanthemum Production Price is High

White chrysanthemum, that is, tea chrysanthemum, is now in the new season. According to a letter from a client in Xieqiao, Haining, the production price is very high, and the market price is 120 yuan per dan.

Coal: White Coal Dust Increases Water Footprint

The white coal dust business is usually only needed by coal ball factories as raw materials for large-scale purchases, and the market price rarely changes. Recently, due to the increase in the water footprint of three shillings, the cost per ton has increased by six yuan. Hongji White Coal No. 1 dust has also risen from 61 yuan to 67 yuan. Retail in Menzhuang is 3 yuan and 6 jiao per dan.

Piece Goods: Nanyang Purchases Printed Cloth Endlessly

The cloth market has risen due to the rising cost of raw materials, yarn and cotton, and the mood is stable. The demand for hoarders and local dye factories is gradually increasing. The market price of fine cloth and fine twill from brands such as Dapeng and Fugui has risen by 2 jiao and a half to 5 jiao per piece, and the price of coarse cloth has risen by 1 jiao to 2 jiao and a half per piece. Bleached and dyed cloth has also risen across the board, with the price increasing by about 5 jiao per piece. The local market has seen particularly strong transactions, totaling more than 2,000 pieces. The Hong Kong syndicate has purchased more than 100 packages of coarse and fine twill. The Yong syndicate has purchased nearly 100 pieces of fine and coarse cloth. Overseas sales continue to be smooth, and the Nanyang syndicate purchases printed cloth endlessly. On the 10th, there were 81 pieces of piece goods shipped to Xiamen and 145 pieces shipped to Hong Kong.

Yesterday, the Eastern cloth market saw continued price increases due to the firm rise of yarn and thread, and the mood was high. The morning opening price of the fine cloth from the White Goods Longtou was 20 yuan and 8 jiao and a half per piece. In the later market, because the industry and hoarders still had strong intentions to buy, the price gradually rose to 21 yuan and 1 jiao and a half. Ito, Dongmian and other companies opened more than 500 pieces of Longtou fine cloth futures, with the price ranging from 21 yuan and 2 jiao and a half to 21 yuan and 5 jiao for this month, and the price for January was even more surprisingly high, ranging from 22 yuan and 5 jiao to 21 yuan and 7 jiao and a half. About 4500 pieces of this month's goods from other brands such as Laba, Wufu, and Caiqiu were opened, with a morning price of 20 yuan per piece and an afternoon price of 20 yuan and 2 jiao and a half. The closing price of the Four Gentlemen Serge was 6 jiao, 6 fen and 7 and a half li per yard.

Sunday Supplement

The Vigorous New Capital

— Ju Chen

Sichuan—Sichuan, whose land area is larger than the mainland of Japan, with its fertile soil, rich products, and superior position... Everyone knows that it is the base of our country's war of resistance; and the key to controlling this base is Ba County (i.e., Chongqing). In the past, Sichuan, apart from Chengdu, Ba County was actually the leader among the 146 counties in the province. In the winter of the 26th year of the Republic of China, the National Government moved into Bashu, and Chongqing became the new capital.

The Area is About to Increase Threefold

Chongqing was established as a city in May of this year (28th year). Its area is about 147 square kilometers. Recently, the suburbs have been incorporated into the city. The preliminary work of surveying the boundaries has been completed, and by the end of this year, the area of the city can be increased three times. With the expansion of the area, the budget will naturally also increase. This year's budget is more than 3 million yuan, and it is expected that the income will increase by 7 million yuan next year. Planning to Build a Ring Road Around the City

Although the Japanese planes are constantly flying back and forth, the government still allocated 10 million yuan to build a ring road around the city, which is expected to be completed in three years. Everyone knows that Chongqing is located on the delta where the Jialing River and the Yangtze River meet, and there is a saying that "there is no three feet of flat land," so it can be said to be a mountainous peninsula. Building roads is naturally doubly difficult. Some places near the valley also need to build 60-foot-high embankments. Therefore, only 30% of this 10 million yuan is used to purchase land, and 70% must be used for engineering, which shows the arduousness of the work and the unremitting spirit of the government authorities. As for transportation with the outside world, it can be said that it is accessible by water, land, and air. This is unnecessary to elaborate on.

The road construction plan is planned to be implemented in the first month of next year, because tax revenue can be increased at that time, and after the road is built, the value of the land will increase. It is also worthwhile to sell the excess land purchased at a low price now, so that the cost of road construction can be recovered. There are quite a few slums along the banks of the two rivers now. In the future, when the road is completed, buses and public buses (also some trams) will be speeding by, which will surely make people feel the vicissitudes of life.

Building Tunnels and Residential Areas

Another plan is to build underground tunnels connecting the downtown area and the southern area to avoid the current labor of detouring on the road. At the same time, it can also be used as an air-raid shelter for millions of yuan. If we start in three places, it will take about six months to complete.

According to the method of dispersing the population, it is planned to build affordable housing areas in the suburbs. The addresses have been selected in several places, and a loan of 3 million yuan has been obtained from the Bank of China as construction costs. In the first phase, it is planned to build four places first, followed by eight places. Each place has a park, a sports field, surrounded by shops and residences. These shops and residences may be built by the municipal government or by the people themselves.

Financial Budget and Population

Chongqing is now the center of transportation in the northwest and southwest, and ferries are also being improved. The population of the city was 500,000 before the bombing, but now it is only 380,000 due to evacuation. If it were not wartime, it could not become a special municipality. According to regulations, a special municipality must have a population of one million to be established and directly under the Executive Yuan.

This year's Chongqing budget is 3.3 million, 32.08% is used for public safety, 25.6% is used for public construction, 11% is used for education and social undertakings, and 31.32% is used for public health. Next year, we plan to add a little more to the education budget.

The vigorous new capital is like an oil pool, the more it is bombed, the more prosperous it becomes. The original Chongqing, "a leaf floating in the country of Ba, with two rivers floating around the Futu Pass," is actually the origin of our nation's "Chongqing" regeneration.

Anecdotes of Life in the New Capital

— Ya Wen

If you come to the new capital and take a look, you will feel infinitely surprised; because the new capital in wartime, although it has been bombed repeatedly, has not only not become a ruin,

Instead, it is becoming more prosperous every day, and the people are showing a solemn and happy appearance. Everyone believes that the time for final victory is not far away. The cars flowing money on the road are endless. The bombed place is immediately covered with bungalows made of bamboo. The land price in the Yushi Street, Wuku Street, Doyou Street, and Quanggongju Street areas has risen to more than 700 yuan per square foot, and the landlord is still unwilling to let go. The goods in the store have everything they should have, as long as you can afford the price, any cosmetics, photographic materials, woolen tweed, canned food, can be bought at will.

Clothing: The clothing of the new urban residents is very simple. The most fashionable for women is to wear cheongsams with blue cloth faces, and Ann Ann blue cloth is in short supply on the face of the new capital. Ordinary men mostly like to wear cloth Zhongshan suits. The labor cost of tailor shops is very expensive. An ordinary three-piece suit, excluding the woolen material, costs no less than 30 yuan in wages; therefore, there are not as many people wearing suits as in Shanghai. Male and female students all wear the prescribed uniforms and walk on the street, which is very neat. Noble women in the new capital do not wear high-heeled leather shoes, because the municipal government stipulates that prostitutes only wear high-heeled leather shoes, so no one is willing to imitate.

Food: In terms of food, in addition to Sichuan restaurants, all other types of restaurants are available. Cantonese cuisine such as Dasanyuan and Guanshengyuan; Suzhou cuisine such as Songhelou, Northern cuisine such as Yanshi Restaurant, Ningbo cuisine with Siming Night Snack Restaurant, Yangzhou cuisine with Slender West Lake, and several Nanjing cuisine restaurants such as Guotai. None of them are not thriving. Every night when the lights come on, there is always no space, spitting out a batch of people and swallowing another batch of people. Although there are also several Western restaurants, the taste is not as good as Shanghai because the production of fresh fish is not high and the refining of cream is not very effective. Several new Russian restaurants have recently opened. A small pot of borscht, slightly served with bread, does not cost much, and can fill the stomach, so many people tend to go there, and the business is quite good.

Transportation: Although the roads in the new capital are not as wide as those in Shanghai, pedestrians can abide by the rules of walking, so although the narrow road is full of pedestrians, there will never be any crowding or conflicts. Especially during gatherings, the masses abide by order, file in, and there is no sound of rushing or shouting. This point has aroused the admiration of foreigners.

Hygiene: The locals in the new capital have a Ni Zan-like cleanliness. There are more bathrooms in the city than in other places, and ordinary bathrooms are equipped with places to receive women, as well as so-called family bathrooms. Ordinary families take their families to bathe together. The bathing fee is calculated by time, ranging from one to two yuan per hour. Now the municipal government is afraid that some people will bring prostitutes to pretend to be family members to take a bath, and for the sake of maintaining customs, it has ordered those who run bathhouses to separate men's and women's bathrooms, not to allow them to bathe together again, and not to allow them to stay overnight.

Foreigners: There are recently more than 360 foreign nationals in the new capital (excluding the Navy), with women accounting for one-third. Most of them are embassy staff and missionaries. The rest are representatives of commercial operations. Since the outbreak of the war with Germany, British, German, and French expatriates have been talking about the news of the war in their home countries in cafes, and they are ready to return to serve their countries at any time.

Air Defense: The air defense deployment in the new capital is extremely thorough. Many new air-raid shelters have been dug, divided into three major areas: the urban area, Jiangbei, and Nan'an, with a total of more than 500 air-raid shelters, which can accommodate more than 60,000 people. In the event of an air raid, the air defense headquarters will issue an alarm with electric sirens, and the people will not panic when they hear the alarm. They will enter the shelter together, and some will carry books and read without stopping in the light of kerosene lamps or flashlights in the air-raid shelter. The calmness of their attitude can be seen.

Chongqing's Products and Commerce

— Shao Tang

Chongqing does not produce much rice, and mostly relies on the supply of neighboring counties. The output of miscellaneous grains such as potatoes, corn, peanuts, sesame and various beans is extremely rich, especially beans, because the climate is earlier than the lower Yangtze River. Even in the winter season, fresh beans can be eaten. In addition, the output of livestock such as chickens and ducks and fruits such as oranges, grapefruit, pears, etc. is also extremely rich. The development of mineral products is very small. Coal is the main product extracted from the nearby mountains; in Shiyougou, Nan'an, there is natural outflow of petroleum that can be used.

The most famous factory is the improved silk factory run by the Sichuan Silk Industry Institute. There are more than 4,000 looms in the city. There is a cement factory in Nan'an with a very large scale, and its output is sufficient for the entire Sichuan province. The bleached bristles produced by the Chuanyu Pig Bristle Factory are sold in Europe and the United States and are especially famous. Since the War of Resistance, according to the Ministry of Economic Affairs, a total of more than 340 factories have moved from Shanghai and Wuhan to the inland, including about 150 machinery and hardware industries, more than 20 electrical and radio industries, about 40 chemical industries, about 10 ceramic and glass industries, about 20 food and beverage industries, 60 textile industries, and more than 40 printing industries. Among them, four-tenths have been moved to Sichuan Province, and some of them have already started construction in Chongqing. There are four yarn factories, namely Qingxin, Yuhua, Yufeng, and Dacheng. According to the industry, there are currently more than 50,000 yarn factories in Chongqing. The main export commodities are tung oil, raw silk, medicinal materials, pig bristles, cow leather, and sheepskin, while the main import commodities are piece goods, cotton yarn, hardware, Soviet goods, and pigments. Among the export commodities, tung oil is the most famous, accounting for the first place in my country's export commodities. In addition to the Juxingcheng Zhongzhongjiaonong four banks, Shanghai Bank and Zhejiang Xingye Bank also have branches. Financial activities are lively, and the atmosphere is new every day.

Transportation in Chongqing

Because Chongqing is surrounded by water on three sides, water transportation is convenient. Foreign ships navigating the Yangtze River westward have always used this as their terminal. Before the war, the two giant ships, "Minyuan" and "Minben," operated by Mr. Lu Zuofu of Sichuan, sailed directly from Chongqing to Shanghai, taking only ten days downstream and no more than two weeks upstream. Due to the current war situation, downstream navigation only reaches Yichang, while upstream navigation reaches Jiading, and northward navigation reaches Hechuan. In addition, there are small steamers traveling to various locations, such as the Yu-Fu Line from Chongqing to Fuling, the Yu-Mu Line from Chongqing to Mudong, the Yu-Song Line from Chongqing to Songgai, the Yu-Wen Line from Chongqing to Wenquan, and the Yu-Ci Line from Chongqing to Ciqikou. The Chengdu-Chongqing Railway is currently under construction but not yet open to traffic. The main highways are divided into westward and southward lines. The westward line runs directly from Chongqing to Chengdu, totaling 450 kilometers, and connects to the northwest highway. The southward line runs directly to Guiyang, totaling 488 kilometers. In addition, there is the Yu-Yuan Highway from Chongqing to Yuanling in Hunan, totaling 993 kilometers, but it is not yet fully open to traffic. There is also a short-distance bus service from Chongqing to Ciqikou, called the Yu-Ci Line. On the Chongqing-Guiyang section, there is also the Haitangxi-Wenquan branch line from Haitangxi in Chongqing to Wenquan. On the Chongqing-Chengdu section, there is also the Qingmuguan-Beibei branch line from Qingmuguan in Chongqing to Beibei. Public buses operated by bus companies run within the city, divided into four routes. One route runs between Zengjiayan and Guojielou, one route runs between Tongjielou and Caiyuanba, one route runs between Daxigou and Hualongqiao, and one route runs between Xiaoshizi and Shangqingsi. The stations along this route were originally part of the first route, but due to the excessive number of passengers on the first route, the fourth route was added to reduce congestion. For commercial aviation, there are two major companies, China National Aviation Corporation and Eurasia Aviation Corporation, both with regular scheduled flights. China National Aviation Corporation flies to Guilin, Hong Kong, Guiyang, Hanoi, Kunming, Luzhou, Xufu, Jiading, Wanxian, Yichang, and Chengdu. Eurasia Aviation Corporation flies to Guilin, Kunming, Hanoi, Chengdu, Hanzhong, Xi'an, Lanzhou, Ningxia, Liangzhou, and Xining. Postal services are under the jurisdiction of the Eastern Sichuan Administration Bureau, with a total of twelve branches distributed throughout the city, in addition to the General Bureau. The telegraph service has now been expanded to form the Sichuan-Kang-Tibet Telegraph Administration Bureau, with an average daily volume of over 1,800 telegrams sent and received, and approximately 7,000 telegrams relayed. International telegrams are usually transmitted via radio or submarine cable, and domestic telegrams are also often transmitted via radio due to line issues. For long-distance calls, in addition to military use,

the Great Buddha by the Jialing River can directly communicate with Chengdu, Shiyang, Neijiang, Jiajiang, Leshan, Qijiang, Wanxian, Liangshan, Changshou, Badong, Dianjiang, Fengjie, Nanwenquan, Kunming, Hong Kong, and other places. This spring, trial wireless telephone calls were also made with Dihua in Xinjiang and Lanzhou in Gansu, with good results, and it is expected that they will be open to the public soon.

Salt Wells in Chongqing

— Huanlan

There is a common saying: "The seven necessities to begin a day are firewood, rice, oil, salt, sauce, vinegar, and tea." Although salt ranks fourth, its importance is no less than that of firewood, rice, or oil. Because everyone needs it, salt tax is a very important item in the national revenue.

Salt includes rock salt, lake salt, and well salt. Sichuan's salt comes from wells, called well salt. A few years ago, there were twenty-three salt fields in the province engaged in production. Statistics show that there were more than 8,800 salt wells, and there are many near Chongqing. Because the brine quality of well salt is weak, on average, evaporating about 20 jin of water is required to produce 1 jin of salt. At a time when fuel is expensive, the cost is also high. According to a report at the end of November this year, a certain chemical industry society introduced the Shinoda drying method from France and Germany and built drying racks, which were tested at the Niuhuaxi salt field with excellent results. This method can save fuel and allow for natural evaporation. It is said that each drying rack costs three to four thousand yuan, but if implemented throughout the province, it could save ten million yuan in fuel costs.

The picture shows a salt well in Chongqing. The wooden frame and wheel disc are the pulleys used to extract brine, which, as physics explains, use fulcrums to reduce labor.

A Brief Record of Chongqing

— Shaotang

Chongqing is located at 106 degrees 37 minutes 48 seconds east longitude and 29 degrees 35 minutes 10 seconds north latitude, with an elevation of 240 feet. It is situated at the confluence of the Jialing River and the Yangtze River, surrounded by water on three sides and connected to land on one side. Strategists consider it a crucial point for both water and land routes, controlling Jing and Kui to the east, pointing to Chengdu to the west, leading to Qian and Dian to the south, and looking to Hanzhong to the north, making its terrain extremely important. In the Zhou Dynasty, it was the State of Ba, with a viscount of the Ji surname. During the Qin and Han dynasties, it was the territory of Ba Commandery. In the Jin Dynasty, it was renamed Badu. At the beginning of the Sui Dynasty, it was renamed Yuzhou. During the reign of Emperor Yang, it was renamed Yu Commandery. In the Tang Dynasty, it was renamed Yuzhou again. It was not until the reign of Emperor Xiaozong of the Song Dynasty that it was renamed Chongqing Prefecture. During the Yuan Dynasty, it was established as Chongqing Circuit. In the Ming Dynasty, it was renamed Chongqing Prefecture again, and this continued in the Qing Dynasty. In the early years of the Republic of China, the prefecture was abolished and replaced by a county. In the twenty-fifth year, a city was established. In the twenty-eighth year, it was changed to a municipality directly under the Executive Yuan of the National Government. The total area of the city is 174 square kilometers. In the sixteenth year of Guangxu (Qing Dynasty), it was permitted as a treaty port due to the Sino-British Beijing Additional Treaty. In the twentieth year of Guangxu (Qing Dynasty), the Treaty of Shimonoseki with Japan designated it as a commercial port.

The Great Buddha Beside the Jialing River

Page 16

Scenic Spots in Chongqing

— Shaotang

Chongqing is surrounded by mountains and rivers, with many scenic spots. The most famous are the North and South Hot Springs. The South Hot Spring is about 40 li from the city. The water source comes from Jianyu Mountain, and the temperature is constantly maintained at 44 degrees Fahrenheit. It contains a lot of sulfur, so it can treat various skin diseases. In addition to the main spring, there are two small springs, one called Ziquan, located in Juewen Garden behind the hot spring resort. The water volume is very small and is not open to the public. The other is called Xiaowenquan, located on the left bank of Huatanxi Creek, about 3 li from the hot spring resort. The North Hot Spring is located in Wentang Gorge downstream of the Jialing River, 140 li by water from Chongqing. The land route is slightly shorter than the water route, only 79.5 kilometers. Tourists can take a bus from Qingmuguan to Beibei if traveling by land, and then take a tourist boat from Beibei Hot Spring Park to directly reach the North Hot Spring. The spring water emerges from the foothills in three streams. The temperature is slightly lower than that of the South Hot Spring, warmer in winter and cooler in summer, unlike the constant temperature of the South Hot Spring throughout the year. According to the chemical analysis results of the Western China Academy of Sciences, the highest temperature of the North Spring is around 37 degrees Celsius. The mineral content, especially lime, is slightly higher, but it can also treat skin diseases. Famous scenic spots near the South Hot Spring include Jianwen Peak. Legend has it that Emperor Jianwen of the Ming Dynasty once hid on this peak. There was originally a Jianwen Temple on the mountain peak, but it has been in disrepair for many years; most of the buildings in the temple have collapsed. Near the North Hot Spring is Gaokeng Rock, where waterfalls fly across. It is over a hundred feet high and nearly two hundred feet wide. People cannot approach within three zhang, making it the most magnificent scenery near the North Hot Spring. In addition, there are also the Twelve Scenic Spots of Bayu, such as Jinbi Liushui and Hongya Dicui, as well as gardens, villas, caves, temples, and other famous scenic spots, too numerous to mention, so they are omitted here.

Huatanxi Creek in the South Hot Spring

Wartime Work of Women in Chongqing—A Spirit of Service Exceeding That of Men—

— Xinmeng

In the streets of Chongqing, one can often see teams of Chinese girls with sun-darkened faces and skin, singing military songs, with blankets and other items on their backs, marching in orderly steps. Under the leadership of Madame Chiang, their lives are disciplined and militarized. Among these women, 450 are from the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. The youngest is only fourteen years old, but she claimed to be fifteen in order to join the Women's Wartime Service Corps. They received military training in Hunan, and now, under the leadership of Madame Chiang, they are engaged in various wartime tasks. In the rear, they are responsible for teaching elementary school students how to sing military songs and how to take precautions during air raids, as well as participating in public gatherings,慰劳征人家庭, and improving relations between the people and the military.

On May 3rd and 4th, Chongqing suffered a brutal bombing by Japanese aircraft, resulting in a total of 5,000 deaths and 1,000 injuries. They participated in various rescue efforts, demonstrating a spirit of service that exceeded that of men. At the same time, near Chongqing, Madame Chiang established a New Life Textile Factory, planning to recruit 1,000 wives and daughters of servicemen, so that they would each have work. Initially, it is half-work and half-study, teaching not only textile skills but also subjects such as music, language, and arithmetic. After graduation, they implement cooperation and can purchase textile machines at half price, with installment payments. Military families can enjoy special discounts when purchasing goods from the factory.

Since the successive fall of Hankou and Guangzhou, at least 10,000 war orphans rescued from the war zones have been brought to Chongqing. The work of relief and education is entirely carried out by women's organizations. Currently, there are many women's organizations in Chongqing, but they are all unified and commanded by the highest women's movement organ. The weather is getting cold, and servicemen urgently need winter clothing, so recently, women in Chongqing have been busy sewing winter clothes. Under the leadership of Madame Chiang, considerable achievements were made in this work in Hankou, so this time it will naturally be no less impressive.

Random Notes on Chongqing

Since the establishment of the Chongqing Municipal Price Assessment Committee, it has been stipulated that the prices in Chongqing shall be based on the market prices on November 2nd of this year, and no increase shall be allowed thereafter. The standard price for high-quality rice is 16 yuan per dan, and the standard price for vegetable oil is 6.6 jiao per jin.

According to a survey by a foreigner named Stein in August of this year, 386 factories that had relocated from Shanghai and Hankou to the vicinity of Chongqing had 65,000 tons of machinery.

On the 9th of this month, the Ministry of Education promoted social education work. In addition to establishing a wartime social education work corps to provide services everywhere, there are over 1,000 students in civilian schools and over 600 students in women's supplementary schools.

The largest air-raid shelter in the country is in Chongqing, capable of accommodating 10,000 people and equipped with air pumps and generators, etc.

The beggars in Chongqing have all been taken in and given military training.

There are twelve scenic spots and historical sites in Chongqing: Central Park, General's Tomb, Luohan Temple, Jiangbei Park, Liyuan Garden, Laojun Cave, Zhenwu Mountain, Nanshan Mountain, Huayan Temple, Laoying Rock, South Hot Spring, and North Hot Spring, etc.

Four New Ministers

— Guanqing

The Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang was recently held in Xindu, Chongqing. Regarding party affairs, four new ministers were appointed. One is the new Minister of Publicity, Mr. Wang Shijie, a native of Hubei, currently 48 years old. He graduated from Beiyang University at an early age and then went to the University of London in the United Kingdom to study economics, education, and political science. Later, he went to the University of Paris in France to study law and obtained a doctorate. After returning to China, he was hired as a professor of constitutional law at Peking University. In 1928, the Ministry of Education hired him as the president of National Wuhan University. He was serious in his work and was deeply appreciated by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. The following year, he became the Minister of Education. The academic community admired him for his integrity and hard work. He is the author of books such as "Comparative Constitutional Law" and "Chinese Slavery." In his youth, he was intelligent and diligent in his studies. During his studies abroad, various Western professors praised him for his quick thinking and studiousness. He is amiable and approachable, and he has been known for his integrity in politics and education.

The second is the new Minister of Organization, Mr. Zhu Jiahua, courtesy name Liuxian, currently 47 years old, a native of Wuxing, Zhejiang, with a Ph.D. in philosophy from the University of Berlin, Germany. After returning to China, he served as a professor at Peking University, Sun Yat-sen University, and National Central University, as well as a member of the Guangdong Provincial Government and Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Minister of Education, Minister of Communications, and Chairman of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund Board of Directors (currently still in office). Mr. Zhu was handsome, erudite, eloquent, responsible, and public-spirited in his youth, and he is a cornerstone of China's young politicians.

The third is the new Minister of Social Affairs, Mr. Wu Tiecheng, a typical soldier and scholar, currently 51 years old, a native of Zhongshan County, Guangdong, born in Jiangxi. He studied in Japan at an early age and was a successful protégé of the Prime Minister. He served as a representative of Jiangxi Province to the National Congress in Nanjing and as a consultant to the Prime Minister. He then served as the Director of the Guangdong Public Security Bureau and Commander of the Military Police. His subordinates were known for their bravery, and were later reorganized into the 17th Division of the National Revolutionary Army. Later, he served as a member of the Central Legislative Yuan and Mayor of Shanghai. When the War of Resistance broke out, he was transferred to serve as the Chairman of the Guangdong Provincial Government. He is good at socializing and is enthusiastic about public welfare and charity. He is tall and has a bold demeanor. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek appreciates him as a versatile and artistic figure.

The fourth is the new Minister of Social Affairs, Mr. Gu Zhenggang, a native of Guizhou. He is very enthusiastic about party affairs and is courageous and responsible in his work. He has served as an alternate member of the Central Executive Committee, Deputy Minister of the Organization Department, and Counselor of the Ministry of Industry. Mr. Gu is honest and hardworking in politics. He is unwilling to let others take the lead in any undertaking that benefits the party, the country, and the people, so the central government relies heavily on him.

The Fog in Chongqing is Worth 30 Million

Once Chongqing enters winter, it is shrouded in fog, which lasts until the early summer of the following year before clearing up. This fog has its disadvantages and advantages. The disadvantage is that when there is heavy fog, there is no sun, and the climate is very bad, making people feel extremely uncomfortable in such an environment. The advantage is that with fog, planes can easily get lost and are also afraid of hitting the surrounding high mountains, which could cause them to crash. Therefore, once winter arrives, there are not many Japanese bombers going to Chongqing. This is a natural weapon against air raids. When Senator Tao Xingzhi gave a speech in Hong Kong this spring, he said, "The fog in Chongqing is worth 30 million." His explanation was: To make Chongqing's air defense comprehensive, at least 100 anti-aircraft guns are needed, and if each gun costs 300,000, then 30 million would be needed. Once Chongqing has fog, the Japanese dare not bomb, so isn't the fog in Chongqing worth 30 million?

Film and Drama in Chongqing

— Yingdai

Due to the war, several film companies moved from Shanghai to Nanjing, and then from Hankou to Chongqing. Famous movie stars of the past have now joined the Chinese spiritual mobilization, reducing their lifestyles to the bare minimum in terms of clothing and food. Actresses playing leading roles currently receive only 60 yuan per month for living expenses. They are extremely busy with various preparations, but they don't seem to care much about the salary. According to locals, the lighting in Chongqing is very bad, and film production sometimes comes to a standstill because of it. It is even said that dogs in Sichuan are terrified and bark wildly when they see the sun in Chongqing, so you can imagine that sometimes it is impossible to film because of the light.

However, some movie stars cherish their time very much, and even if they are not filming movies, they will use their spare time to do some work. Especially those who have performed in stage plays in the past join legitimate theater troupes and perform wartime dramas in Chongqing and neighboring towns to awaken the general public. Currently, there are many theater groups in Chongqing—professional, amateur, and organized by young students—all standing on the same front line to perform national salvation dramas and engage in theater movements, working quite hard, so there is almost always a theater group performing every day.

Since the outbreak of the European war, foreign exchange has gradually tightened, and not only has the supply of photography materials decreased, but the price has also become very expensive, which has greatly increased the cost of filmmaking. However, film companies in Chongqing, especially "China Film" and "Central Film," are actively proceeding with filmmaking. All the films they shoot contain a sense of resistance. Currently, the films shown in large and small cities in southwestern China are all of this kind. Here, it is not difficult to see that the film and drama movement in Chongqing is being vigorously promoted!

Children's Weekly

The Problem of Children's Crime

— Qiulang

Since the outbreak of the war, Shanghai, known as an isolated island, has produced many war orphans. Although they are taken in and cared for by various charities, the number is too large to accommodate. Therefore, one can see wandering children everywhere in the streets and alleys. These poor children, some still have parents, but they became separated from their homes after the upheaval and scattered along the way. Some don't even have parents. Their lives are so miserable! Every day they wander the streets, scavenging, begging, and even committing theft. The wandering children who commit theft are certainly committing crimes, but because of their young age and lack of knowledge, and because they are under the legal age, the law usually deals with them leniently on the grounds of youth and ignorance.

However, the situation in the "History of Crime by Street Children" recently published in this newspaper is different. According to what was published the other day: "Shanghai street child Lin Meiyuan, thirteen years old, recently stole valuable items on Nanjing Road and was arrested and sent to court. The judge, considering that the child was young, transferred him to the Children's Protection Section of the Public Works Department. According to the child's own statement: his uncle Lin Changchun brought him to Shanghai from Duobo and taught him how to steal. He had to steal items, and the uncle sold them and spent the money himself. Sometimes when he didn't want to steal, his uncle would beat him until he submitted." This is truly outrageous! The child Lin knew that stealing was a criminal act and did not want to do it, but this rogue uncle insisted on instigating him, beating and coercing him for his own gain. The commission of this crime was entirely caused by the rogue uncle, who should be arrested and severely punished! And this child Lin is innocent by nature and capable of being reformed!

Stealing is an immoral and criminal act, let alone teaching ignorant children to embark on a path of crime, while oneself remains free from the law. This is an extremely heinous crime! However, there are adults in society who steal, and children learn from them. There are not many children like Lin who can awaken themselves and distinguish between good and evil. It is hoped that those responsible for society will guide children with pure natures onto the right path from an early age, so as to prevent them from becoming evildoers as adults and leading others to do the same.

Common Sense Questions and Answers

— Chen Zhijun

Q: Why does the bitten area of peaches and pears turn yellowish-brown?

(A) Peaches, pears, and other fruits contain a lot of iron. After we bite off the skin, the iron comes into contact with the air and undergoes oxidation, thus changing color.

(Q) Why does hot water clean better than cold water when washing clothes?

(A) Particles of dirt often stick to clothes and skin with a film of oil. Hot water can soften and dissolve this film of oil in the water, making it cleaner.

(Q) Why does river water flow slower on both sides than in the center?

(A) The water on both sides is slowed down by the resistance of sand and soil on the banks. The water in the center has less resistance, so it flows faster.

(Q) Why does the sun appear larger in the morning and smaller at noon?

(A) In the morning, sunlight shines on the ground at a shallow angle, passing through a very thick layer of air before reaching the eyes. The light is no longer very strong. When our eyes receive this light, the pupils do not need to contract, so they appear larger. At noon, the sun shines directly on the horizon, and the layer of air it passes through is thinner than in the morning. The light shining on the ground is very strong. Our pupils must contract to receive this light, and after the pupils contract, things appear smaller. However, for everyday objects, because of visual perception, the pupils contract the same amount regardless of distance.

(Q) Why do flowers smell sweeter after rain?

(A) There are two reasons: (1) After it rains, the air is fresh, and the fragrance is noticeably stronger.

(2) After it rains, the pores in the flowers that release fragrance are washed clean, allowing them to release more fragrance, so flowers smell sweeter after rain.

(Q) Why do we still have to exert force when swallowing food?

(A) There is air in the stomach, and swallowing requires overcoming its pressure, so exertion is needed.

Wildfire—Ming'er's Refugee Diary, Part 46—

— Baizheng

Watching the sun rise gradually from the mountain crevice in the east and slowly sink behind the hills in the west, another day passed like this. Sleeping and eating, eating and sleeping, wasting the days away in a daze. The climate also changed from warm to warm with the days, indicating that winter was passing and spring was coming. The organisms on the ground, brewing their new lives from the dead corpses, slightly awakened and showed a glimmer of life.

Mountain peaks, the ground, among the hills, by the streams, everywhere there were remnants of tangled and withered weeds, dead branches, barren rice stalks, and withered old leaves. How pitiful! These relics of nature were not collected. Some decayed, others were trampled, all a desolate scene.

After this long winter, spring finally came. The withered grass and fallen leaves could not rot completely, nor could they be trampled all away; they still densely covered the earth, seemingly wanting to last forever, remaining in the vast wilderness. But as winter passed and spring came, their descendants grew again, but they were squeezed by the remnants, unable to move freely, giving their descendants a blow to their lives. The people in the village seemed to understand this very well. Naturally, when this time came, no one went into the mountains to chop firewood anymore, forming an unwritten law. If these tens of thousands of withered grasses were allowed to lie crisscrossed, and new grass grew on top of them in the future, it would hinder the fields they cultivated. If all these grasses were cut away, it would be no easy task. Therefore, during this lean time, there was a grand burning of the mountains.

In recent days, one could find posters plastered on the walls of the village's ancestral hall: Banning the burning of mountains, one is to protect trees, and the other is to reveal the targets of aircraft bombing. But let the posters be posted, the mountains cannot but be burned. This kind of lip service leaves people helpless.

It was a pitch-black night. Just after Ming'er's family finished dinner, they discovered a ball of blazing light at the foot of the mountain opposite their house, like a ball of fire rolling around in the surrounding darkness, appearing particularly dazzling. The ball of fire gradually rolled towards the mountainside, and its area also expanded. Sparks flew in all directions, and the tongues of fire licked the ground, blood-red, licking at what it wanted to devour. The light flickered, eliminating the darkness without a trace, recklessly doing what it wanted within its sphere of influence. The withered grass had already been dried by the wind and sun and was extremely dry. All it took was a spark to ignite it. A wisp of white smoke and flames transformed its withered yellow original appearance into a pile of black ashes, and a gust of wind drove it away to who knows where. The flames spread more violently, and the tongues of fire had an endless ambition, desperately expanding to the places nearby. The crackling of trees, the burning of weeds, and the roaring of flames, along with the shouting of the east wind, formed a symphony of nature. The flames devoured this large area of withered grass like a wild bull. It even spread to and set fire to a small hill. A bright glow illuminated Ming'er, who was standing in the house watching, very brightly, but the wildfire was still unstoppable, but in the end, it had its dead end. Soon it was extinguished.

The foot of the mountain became a scorched earth, seemingly having been baptized by artillery fire. Ming'er remotely thought of that beautiful land! He couldn't help but feel a burst of melancholy! The flames of aggression will eventually be extinguished! And new life can still be built from the scorched earth!

The Donkey and the Nightingale

— Krylov's Fable — Translated by Zhao Yilin

One day, a donkey saw a nightingale. He said to the nightingale, "My dear, listen to me: they say you sing very well, and I have long wanted to hear you sing, to see if what you sing is as good as they say?" The nightingale, hearing this, began to sing. It sang in various tones, melodious and harmonious, moving from one song to another. At one moment, the sound was extremely low, and the distant reeds echoed softly; at another, a delicate melody scattered through the forest, and almost everyone listened to these songs. A breeze blew, and the birds stopped; the cows lay down in the grass. The shepherd boy, listening to the song, also held his breath, smiling at the shepherdess as he listened.

Finally, the song stopped. Then the donkey bowed its head to the ground and criticized, "I found it very unpleasant to listen to! To be honest, no one who hears your singing will not feel tired. It's a pity you haven't heard our rooster crow; if you learned from the rooster, you could sing better..."

The nightingale, hearing this, ignored him and had already flown far away.

The Blue Dwarf (11)

— Ai Li

The dwarf, seeing that Ali had nothing to say, said again, "Dinner is ready, and they are waiting?" Ali turned around and saw a house over there, much larger than the others, its height just enough for her to bend over and enter. When she looked into the house through the window, she saw a long table, covered with a light blue cloth, on which were placed many delicate plates, and next to the plates were a knife, a fork, and a small blue glass. At both ends of the table were two large plates, steaming with a wonderful aroma, which wafted out of the window. Ali smelled the aroma and thought, "I don't feel hungry, but since they have invited me to eat, I might as well accept their hospitality, but I hope they don't ask me to eat pine nuts from the pine trees." The dwarf seemed to know what she meant and said, "They will definitely prepare something good for you to eat." Then he let out a sharp whistle, breaking the silence, and in an instant, the dwarfs in the whole village appeared before her eyes as if by magic, rushing into the house, but as soon as they entered the corridor, they stood on both sides, leaving a path in the middle. The dwarf from before bowed very politely and said, "Please come in."

Ali asked happily, "Do you all gather together like this when you have dinner? How interesting!" The dwarf replied, "Not always, only for public banquets. Please come in and sit down, girl." Ali then stopped speaking, lowered her head, and carefully prepared to enter the door, but suddenly, she heard another sharp whistle, which startled her. She looked up, but bumped hard into the lintel with a bang, which hurt terribly. Immediately, she was annoyed and shouted, "What—what's going on? Why did you whistle again for no reason, startling me? I—" She had no more to say. The sound of the whistle came again, waking Ali up; she had been dreaming.

Ali was dubious, not knowing whether she was awake or dreaming. She stared around, seeing only darkness, her body stiff and cold, and her head still throbbing, because she had just bumped into the old tree trunk. She composed herself, and then heard the sound of a whistle in the distance; it was the early-rising bird starting to sing. The dwarf's whistle that she had heard in her dream was actually the bird's call.

She sobbed to herself, "Oh! Oh! What am I going to do? Where is my body? How can I find my way back in this darkness? Oh, I know, it must be those blue dwarfs playing tricks and making fun of me, making me believe I am dreaming. I knew those dwarfs were also monsters; I shouldn't have followed them to the village." Then she sat quietly for several more minutes, half-asleep, half-awake, still crouching next to the old tree, as if wanting it to protect her. After more time had passed, her consciousness gradually returned, and she thought that sitting still was not a solution; she had to find a way to return to the small inn, thinking that her uncle and aunt were worrying about her, not knowing where she had gotten lost. Thinking of this, she almost burst into tears.

Poor Ali finally struggled to stand up, then remembered the book and umbrella she had brought. She reached out and felt the ground, and they were still by the tree. She hurriedly picked them up, tucked them under her arm, and staggered a few steps forward, thinking that if she walked out of the shade of the trees, it wouldn't be so dark. This did not disappoint her; after she moved away from the old tree, she did feel a little brighter, but the night was still dark, and she could not see a glimmer of dawn. In such darkness, finding a way out of the forest was not easy; she regretted having rashly entered the forest in the first place.

Entertainment World

Searching for the Orphan and Saving the Orphan (Part 1)

— Su Shaoqing

"The Eight Righteousnesses" depicts the history of the rise and fall of the Zhao family of the Jin Kingdom during the Spring and Autumn period. From Zhao Xuanzi to Zhao Wuzi, the Zhao family suffered repeated hardships, but were saved by righteous people, so they were preserved. The legend says that Cheng Ying painted the Zhao family's suffering and the righteous deeds of the eight righteous people into pictures, so that the Zhao family could see them and know the whole story. At that time, Zhao Wu was fifteen years old, strong and powerful. After seeing the pictures, he was able to take revenge. Kunqu often sings scenes such as "Trouble in the Court," "Striking the Dog," "Saving the Orphan," and "Viewing the Paintings," which depict this story. The "Searching for the Orphan and Saving the Orphan" performed in the Erhuang opera is based on the Yuan Dynasty zaju. The Yuanqu Selection has "Zhao's Orphan," which tells the story of Cheng Ying and Gongsun Chujiu saving the orphan. The Erhuang opera starts from the two men's plan, without Han Jue's suicide in front and revenge in the back, so it is not a complete opera. If the whole play is not performed, it cannot be named "The Eight Righteousnesses" in general, but only "Searching for the Orphan and Saving the Orphan."

Now, the Pihuang opera only performs "Searching for the Orphan and Saving the Orphan" because the plot of saving the orphan is the best, extremely emotional, and the used wisdom is beyond human emotion. Cheng's wife can't bear to give up her swaddled child, and Chujiu implies that Cheng Ying must do it reluctantly. Compared to "Changing Children at the Execution Ground," Xu Ce kneels down, and Xu's family gives up her own child to be loyal. The tactics are like links, emerging endlessly. Cheng Ying exposes Chujiu first, one thing; and whips him personally, two things; the orphan is searched out by Tu Anjia in person (according to historical records, after Tu Anjia killed Zhao Shuo, Zhao Kuo, etc., he repeatedly searched Zhao Shuo's wife in the palace. Shuo's wife, the daughter of Duke Jin, gave birth to an orphan, and Shuo's wife prayed to heaven, ordering the child not to cry, and if there was a sound, the Zhao family would be cut off. Tu searched for a long time, and the child was silent, so he was spared. Tu continued to search urgently, and Han Jue was ordered by Tu to guard the palace gate. Cheng Ying carried the orphan out in a medicine box and was searched out by Han. Cheng cried and begged very sadly, and Han let him go and committed suicide. Now Tu's search is the third search. If the whole play is arranged, three searches for Zhao's orphan will be more interesting), making him not suspicious, three things; Chujiu dies with the fake orphan, making Tu relieved, four things; Cheng Ying and the real orphan return to Tu's mansion for upbringing, five things; the five plans are all beyond human emotion, so even if the Tu thief is ruthless, he doesn't realize he's in the drum.

In the play, Cheng Ying begs his wife to give up her child, even kneeling down and holding a knife to her throat, which is interesting, but this is the organization of the drama. According to the historical records, "Gongsun Chujiu falsely carried another infant and hid in the mountains." The fake orphan who died with Chujiu was the child of an unknown family, not Cheng Ying's own child. The play says that it is Cheng's child, which adds a lot of drama and makes it more intimate and outstanding. This is the best organization method, and it can be said that it is Cheng's own child.

The Erhuang opera also has a complete version of this play, with scenes of viewing paintings and revenge fifteen years after searching for the orphan. Tan school old student amateur actor Wang Yutian once recorded the Erhuang Yuanban lyrics of Cheng Ying in "The Eight Righteousnesses" on a Baidai Diamond phonograph record, "Hiding the orphan in the empty mountain, it has been fifteen years now, in my heart I only hate the traitor, who harmed the Zhao family like that, alas, my brother Gongsun gave his life, alas, I am half a hundred years old and have no son, if God opens his eyes three points, revenge will be avenged, and injustice will be redressed," which is the singing before revenge. (Wang Yutian's voice is sad and suitable for singing Erhuang tunes, most like the old Tan, and his skills are also good. He once went to sea to perform in operas and died in Tianjin at the age of only forty.)

Miscellaneous Writings on the Art Scene

— Hua

The Dahua Grand Theater is scheduled to open on the evening of the second day, presenting Miguel Lona and Judy Garland's "Meet Me in St. Louis." This afternoon at 7:30, the theater will host all sectors and preview the new film.

As everyone knows, the four first-run Western film theaters in Shanghai are now completely under the jurisdiction of the Asia Cinema, so during the holidays, they no longer compete with each other as they did in the past, selecting and screening giant films that compete with each other. Now, the Dahua Grand Theater has risen up and won the premiere rights of MGM, which produces the most films every year, so the programming of the Daguangming and Nanjing theaters will have to be considered. (The Cathay is mostly attended by Western audiences, and the Da Shanghai has now implicitly lowered its level by half, so there is no problem.)

At the end of 1939, after "The Regret of the Late Ming Dynasty," another major event occurred in the drama world. That was the reorganization of the "Improved Civilization Drama." Veteran dramatist Wei Ruhui, Yu Ling and Zhou Yibai, etc., joined the Green Treasure Theater as screenwriters at the introduction of Gu Menghu. Since Tan Zhiyuan, Gu Menghu, Bai Hong, etc. first proposed the slogan of "Improved Civilization Drama," although they also encountered many setbacks, under the hard work of Gu Menghu, the Green Treasure Theater, which had always been regarded by the drama world as a civilization drama, actually established a sound foundation of a large audience. Recently, many dramatists have realized that striving for civilization drama is not a fall, especially to educate the ladies and grandmothers, they should break into the corrupt circle of life, "If I don't go to hell, who will?" Veteran dramatists such as Yu Ling and Zhou Yibai personally took the stage, which could also serve as a wake-up call for general patients with "shallow thinking."

Weekly Question and Answer

Sixth Game, Whimsical, Red Loses First

— Published by Xue Weihan

This game is sometimes encountered during Go, and is often drawn. I think this game is indeed a black win, so I recorded and published it for research.

Announcement (1) This column welcomes answers, with a one-week limit. The first seven people will be slightly rewarded. Please send letters to No. 3, Liuhe Village, Moliai Road. (3) The first correct respondents in the previous issue were Wang Zhongsheng, Li Guanghui, Ban Nongfu, Li Jingming, Ge Fuzhi, Bao Hanliang, and Cao Wenxuan.
